## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth terms where the growth rate depends on current population size, possibly with time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (1 + c3) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (logistic with time-dependent rate)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with competition saturation)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → Polynomial in P: terms like P*(1 - c*P) indicate logistic-type self-limitation
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic terms in P: P*(P-a)*(K-P) structure with sign changes
- Logarithmic growth deceleration → P*log(K/P) structure indicates Gompertz-type slower approach to carrying capacity
- Metabolic scaling in growth → Fractional power laws P^(2/3) or P^(3/4) reflecting surface-to-volume or metabolic scaling
- Seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing → Multiplicative trigonometric modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth terms
- Competitive exclusion / resource limitation → Rational forms P/(1+c*P) representing saturating resource uptake
- Time-lagged effects approximated → Polynomial corrections in t multiplied by population terms
- Extinction threshold behavior → Multiplicative factor (P - c_threshold) creating zero-crossing at critical population
- Carrying capacity as ratio → Growth rate structure c0*P - c1*P^2 where K = c0/c1 emerges as equilibrium
- Multiple equilibria → Odd-degree polynomials in P (cubic, quintic) allowing multiple stable/unstable fixed points
